## Task P10 — Create the negative fixture + test: NO_WORKFLOW_RUN end-to-end

**File 1 (new fixture):** `docs/research/fixtures/sample-run-no-workflow.jsonl`

A direct-answer stream: a `session`, a turn that emits assistant text, and **no**
`tool_execution_end(toolName="workflow")`. Write exactly these lines (one JSON object per
line, no trailing blank line semantics required):

```
{"type":"session","version":3,"id":"019ea300-0000-7000-8000-000000000001","timestamp":"2026-06-07T17:00:00.000Z","cwd":"/root/pi-mcp"}
{"type":"agent_start"}
{"type":"turn_start"}
{"type":"message_start"}
{"type":"text","text":"The Earth orbits the Sun — answered directly without any workflow."}
{"type":"message_end"}
{"type":"turn_end"}
{"type":"agent_end"}
```

> Rationale: mirrors §10 ("resposta direta sem `tool_execution_end(workflow)` →
> NO_WORKFLOW_RUN"). The only difference from the positive fixture is the **absence** of the
> workflow `tool_execution_*` pair.

**File 2 (test):** append to `internal/parser/fixture_test.go`

```go
func TestParseStream_NegativeFixture_NoWorkflowRun(t *testing.T) {
	f, err := os.Open(fixturePath(t, "sample-run-no-workflow.jsonl"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	defer f.Close()

	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ParseStream error: %v", err)
	}
	if got.SessionID != "019ea300-0000-7000-8000-000000000001" {
		t.Fatalf("SessionID = %q", got.SessionID)
	}
	if got.WorkflowFound {
		t.Fatal("WorkflowFound = true, want false")
	}
	if e := got.Err(); e != config.ErrNoWorkflowRun {
		t.Fatalf("Err() = %q, want %q", e, config.ErrNoWorkflowRun)
	}
	if len(got.Result) != 0 {
		t.Fatalf("Result = %q, want empty", string(got.Result))

}
```

## Task P11 — Failing test: workflow ran but `isError:true` is surfaced (not NO_WORKFLOW_RUN)

(the parser found a workflow run; failure is the caller's concern per §9 extraction order).

```go
func TestParseStream_WorkflowIsError(t *testing.T) {
	const in = `{"type":"session","id":"s-err"}
{"type":"tool_execution_start","toolName":"workflow"}
{"type":"tool_execution_end","toolName":"workflow","isError":true,"result":{"content":[{"type":"text","text":"WORKFLOW_ABORTED: aborted by user"}]}}
`
	got, err := ParseStream(context.Background(), strings.NewReader(in))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ParseStream error: %v", err)
	}
	if !got.WorkflowFound {
		t.Fatal("WorkflowFound = false, want true")
	}
	if !got.IsError {
		t.Fatal("IsError = false, want true")
	}
	if e := got.Err(); e != "" {
		t.Fatalf("Err() = %q, want \"\" (workflow present, just failed)", e)
	}
	if got.RawText != "WORKFLOW_ABORTED: aborted by user" {
		t.Fatalf("RawText = %q", got.RawText)
	}
}
```

**Run (expect PASS — P3 already records IsError and RawText):**


NO_WORKFLOW_RUN. If FAIL, the bug is conflating IsError with WorkflowFound — fix in P3 logic.)

## internal/runstore — read run files, parse to model.Run, authoritative .result, model histogram, journal↔agents join, pi_list (`runstore`)

**Files:** internal/runstore/runstore.go, internal/runstore/runstore_test.go, internal/runstore/histogram.go, internal/runstore/histogram_test.go, internal/runstore/intermediate.go, internal/runstore/intermediate_test.go, internal/runstore/list.go, internal/runstore/list_test.go, internal/runstore/result.go, internal/runstore/result_test.go, internal/runstore/testdata/sample-run.json, internal/runstore/testdata/sample-run-partial.json, internal/runstore/testdata/sample-run-corrupt.json, internal/runstore/testdata/sample-run-corrupt.json.bak, docs/research/fixtures/sample-run-partial.json

_Assumptions:_ No Go toolchain is installed in THIS build env (`go version` -> not found); every `go test`/`go build`/`go vet` command in the plan runs where Go 1.23+ IS installed. Each test step states the exact command + expected FAIL/PASS so the executor can verify against real output.; Package `pi-mcp/internal/model` (Run, Agent, JournalEntry, TokenUsage, IntermediateResult, StatusMetadata, ListItem, ListOutput) and `pi-mcp/internal/config` (MaxInlineResultBytes=16*1024) are owned by the foundation/model package owner and land BEFORE runstore tasks. runstore imports and builds EXACTLY against the contract signatures; it never defines or renames them. Task R1.1 is a guard that fails clearly if internal/model is absent.; go.mod with `module pi-mcp` is created by the foundation package (Task 1 of the overall plan). If running runstore tasks standalone, `go mod init pi-mcp` first.; Tests use a hermetic copy of the canonical fixture at internal/runstore/testdata/sample-run.json (not the repo-root docs path) so `go test ./...` works from any cwd. The new sample-run-partial.json is authored in BOTH docs/research/fixtures/ (spec Fase 0 deliverable) and internal/runstore/testdata/ (for tests).; by_model histogram keys are the FULL verbatim model id from agents[].model ('deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash', 'openai-codex/gpt-5.5'); the spec's {flash:3,gpt-5.5:1} is human shorthand. ByModel maps assert the verbatim-key form.; Status disk->terminal mapping and liveness/staleness live in internal/jobs, NOT runstore. runstore returns the raw run-file status and parsed Run; consumers apply mapping. Keeps runstore side-effect-free and unit-testable against fixtures.; Cost is read verbatim from tokenUsage.cost as float64, never recomputed. ListItem.Cost / StatusMetadata.TokenUsage are nil when tokenUsage is omitted (running/failed runs).; pi_list sort key is updatedAt desc; runs missing updatedAt sort last (zero time); ties broken by runId for determinism. The two test fixtures share an updatedAt timestamp so the tie-break path is exercised.; ReadRun falls back to a sibling <path>.bak only when the primary is corrupt/missing AND the .bak decodes; corrupt-with-no-usable-.bak returns an error (ReadRun) or is skipped (ListRuns). *.tmp and *.bak are excluded from the ListRuns glob via suffix checks.

# Package R — `internal/runstore`

Reads `<cwd>/.pi/workflows/runs/*.json`, decodes into `model.Run`, exposes: authoritative `.result` (when `status=completed`), the `by_model` histogram, the live `intermediate[]` list (JOIN `journal[].index == agents[].callIndex`), and the `pi_list` listing (sort `updatedAt` desc). Pure I/O + parse + join — no status mapping, no liveness (those live in `internal/jobs`).

**Contract used (verbatim, do not redefine):**
- `model.Run`, `model.Agent`, `model.JournalEntry`, `model.TokenUsage` (§7).
- `model.IntermediateResult{ Label, Model, Phase string; Result json.RawMessage; Preview string; Truncated bool }`.
- `model.StatusMetadata{ ByModel map[string]int; AgentCount int; TokenUsage *TokenUsage; DurationMs *int64 }`.
- `model.ListItem{ RunID, WorkflowName, Status string; AgentCount int; ByModel map[string]int; Cost *float64; DurationMs *int64; CompletedAt *time.Time }` and `model.ListOutput{ Runs []ListItem }`.
- `config.MaxInlineResultBytes = 16*1024`.
- JOIN RULE: `journal[i].Index == agents[j].CallIndex` (NEVER array position, NEVER `agents.ID` which = CallIndex+1). Journal is ordered by completion (e.g. 0,2,1,3).

> **Go-presence note:** `go` is NOT installed in the build env. Every `go ...` command below runs where Go 1.23+ IS installed. Run from repo root `/root/pi-mcp` (module `pi-mcp` already initialized by the foundation package). If running standalone first: `go mod init pi-mcp`.

---

```go
package runstore

import (
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"
)

func TestReadRun_Canonical(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	if r.RunID != "mq40rdpt-yij9hj" {
		t.Errorf("RunID = %q, want mq40rdpt-yij9hj", r.RunID)
	}
	if r.Status != "completed" {
		t.Errorf("Status = %q, want completed", r.Status)
	}
	if r.WorkflowName != "judge_claims" {
		t.Errorf("WorkflowName = %q, want judge_claims", r.WorkflowName)
	}
	if len(r.Agents) != 4 {
		t.Fatalf("len(Agents) = %d, want 4", len(r.Agents))
	}
	if len(r.Journal) != 4 {
		t.Fatalf("len(Journal) = %d, want 4", len(r.Journal))
	}
	// Journal is in completion order, not array position: 0,2,1,3.
	gotOrder := []int{r.Journal[0].Index, r.Journal[1].Index, r.Journal[2].Index, r.Journal[3].Index}
	want := []int{0, 2, 1, 3}
	for i := range want {
		if gotOrder[i] != want[i] {
			t.Errorf("Journal index order[%d] = %d, want %d", i, gotOrder[i], want[i])
		}
	}
	if r.TokenUsage == nil {
		t.Fatal("TokenUsage = nil, want non-nil")
	}
	if r.TokenUsage.Cost != 0.1463847 {
		t.Errorf("Cost = %v, want 0.1463847 (verbatim)", r.TokenUsage.Cost)
	}
	if r.DurationMs == nil || *r.DurationMs != 22391 {
		t.Errorf("DurationMs = %v, want 22391", r.DurationMs)
	}
}

func TestReadRun_PartialOmitsOptionals(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run-partial.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	if r.Status != "running" {
		t.Errorf("Status = %q, want running", r.Status)
	}
	if r.CompletedAt != nil {
		t.Errorf("CompletedAt = %v, want nil (omitted)", r.CompletedAt)
	}
	if r.DurationMs != nil {
		t.Errorf("DurationMs = %v, want nil (omitted)", r.DurationMs)
	}
	if r.TokenUsage != nil {
		t.Errorf("TokenUsage = %v, want nil (omitted)", r.TokenUsage)
	}
	if len(r.Result) != 0 {
		t.Errorf("Result = %s, want empty (omitted)", r.Result)
	}
	if r.CurrentPhase == nil || *r.CurrentPhase != "Scan" {
		t.Errorf("CurrentPhase = %v, want Scan", r.CurrentPhase)
	}
}

func TestReadRun_CorruptFallsBackToBak(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run-corrupt.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun (expected .bak fallback): %v", err)
	}
	if r.RunID != "corrupt-recovered" {
		t.Errorf("RunID = %q, want corrupt-recovered (from .bak)", r.RunID)
	}
}

func TestReadRun_CorruptNoBakErrors(t *testing.T) {
	_, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "does-not-exist.json"))
	if err == nil {
		t.Fatal("ReadRun on missing file: err = nil, want error")
	}
}
```

**R2.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**

```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestReadRun
```
Expected FAIL: `undefined: ReadRun`.

**R2.3 — Minimal impl.** Append to `internal/runstore/runstore.go`:
```go
import (
	"encoding/json"
	"fmt"
	"os"

	"pi-mcp/internal/model"
)

// ReadRun decodes a single run file at path into a *model.Run. If the primary
// file is missing or contains invalid JSON, it transparently falls back to a
// sibling "<path>.bak" when one exists (pi writes .bak snapshots). It never
// reads *.tmp. The returned Run has optional fields left nil/empty when omitted.
func ReadRun(path string) (*model.Run, error) {
	r, err := decodeRunFile(path)
	if err == nil {
		return r, nil
	}
	// Fallback: sibling .bak (corrupt or missing primary).
	bak := path + ".bak"
	if r2, err2 := decodeRunFile(bak); err2 == nil {
		return r2, nil
	}
	return nil, fmt.Errorf("runstore: read %s: %w", path, err)
}

func decodeRunFile(path string) (*model.Run, error) {
	b, err := os.ReadFile(path)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}
	var r model.Run
	if err := json.Unmarshal(b, &r); err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("decode %s: %w", path, err)
	}
	return &r, nil
}
```
> Merge the new `import (...)` block with the package clause already in the file (single `package runstore` + one import group).

**R2.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestReadRun -v
```
Expected PASS: all four `TestReadRun*` subtests OK.

**R2.5 — Commit.**
```
git add internal/runstore/runstore.go internal/runstore/runstore_test.go
git commit -m "runstore: ReadRun decodes run file with .bak fallback on corrupt"
```

## Task R3 — `ModelHistogram`: `by_model` from `agents[].model`

**R3.1 — Failing test.** Write `internal/runstore/histogram_test.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"
)

func TestModelHistogram_Canonical(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	got := ModelHistogram(r)
	want := map[string]int{
		"deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash": 3, // the spec's {flash:3}
		"openai-codex/gpt-5.5":       1, // the spec's {gpt-5.5:1}
	}
	if len(got) != len(want) {
		t.Fatalf("histogram = %v, want %v", got, want)
	}
	for k, v := range want {
		if got[k] != v {
			t.Errorf("histogram[%q] = %d, want %d", k, got[k], v)
		}
	}
}

func TestModelHistogram_SkipsEmptyModel(t *testing.T) {
	// Partial run: running agent (callIndex 1) still has a model; agents with
	// empty model strings must not create a "" bucket.
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run-partial.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	got := ModelHistogram(r)
	if _, ok := got[""]; ok {
		t.Errorf("histogram has empty-string key: %v", got)
	}
	if got["deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash"] != 3 {
		t.Errorf("histogram[flash] = %d, want 3", got["deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash"])
	}
}

func TestModelHistogram_Empty(t *testing.T) {
	got := ModelHistogram(&modelRunNoAgents)
	if len(got) != 0 {
		t.Errorf("histogram = %v, want empty map", got)
	}
}
```
> `modelRunNoAgents` is a tiny zero-agent `model.Run` declared in this test file — add at top of file:
```go
import "pi-mcp/internal/model"

var modelRunNoAgents = model.Run{RunID: "empty", Status: "running"}
```
(Place the `import` in the file's import group with `path/filepath` and `testing`.)

**R3.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestModelHistogram
```
Expected FAIL: `undefined: ModelHistogram`.

**R3.3 — Minimal impl.** Write `internal/runstore/histogram.go`:
```go
package runstore

import "pi-mcp/internal/model"

// ModelHistogram counts agents per model id, keyed by the verbatim agents[].model
// string (e.g. "deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash"). Agents with an empty model string
// are skipped so no "" bucket appears. Returns a non-nil (possibly empty) map.
func ModelHistogram(r *model.Run) map[string]int {
	h := make(map[string]int, len(r.Agents))
	for i := range r.Agents {
		m := r.Agents[i].Model
		if m == "" {
			continue
		}
		h[m]++
	}
	return h
}
```

**R3.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestModelHistogram -v
```
Expected PASS.

**R3.5 — Commit.**
```
git add internal/runstore/histogram.go internal/runstore/histogram_test.go
git commit -m "runstore: ModelHistogram (by_model) keyed by verbatim model id"
```

## Task R4 — `Intermediates`: JOIN `journal[].index == agents[].callIndex`, handle out-of-order + truncation

**R4.1 — Failing test.** Write `internal/runstore/intermediate_test.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"encoding/json"
	"path/filepath"
	"strings"
	"testing"

	"pi-mcp/internal/config"
)

func TestIntermediates_JoinByCallIndexNotPosition(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	got := Intermediates(r, config.MaxInlineResultBytes)
	if len(got) != 4 {
		t.Fatalf("len(intermediate) = %d, want 4", len(got))
	}
	// Journal[0] has Index 0 -> must join to agent callIndex 0 ("claim A").
	// Journal[1] has Index 2 -> must join to agent callIndex 2 ("claim C"),
	// NOT to agents[1] ("claim B") and NOT via id (id=callIndex+1).
	if got[0].Label != "claim A" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[0].Label = %q, want claim A", got[0].Label)
	}
	if got[1].Label != "claim C" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Label = %q, want claim C (journal index 2, NOT array pos 1)", got[1].Label)
	}
	if got[1].Model != "deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Model = %q, want deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash", got[1].Model)
	}
	if got[1].Phase != "Scan" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Phase = %q, want Scan", got[1].Phase)
	}
	// Result must be the COMPLETE journal[].result, not the agent resultPreview.
	var parsed struct {
		Claim   string `json:"claim"`
		Verdict string `json:"verdict"`
	}
	if err := json.Unmarshal(got[1].Result, &parsed); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("intermediate[1].Result not valid JSON: %v", err)
	}
	if parsed.Verdict != "TRUE" || !strings.Contains(parsed.Claim, "7 is a prime") {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Result = %s, want the claim-C journal result", got[1].Result)
	}
	if got[1].Truncated {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Truncated = true, want false (under limit)")
	}
}

func TestIntermediates_Partial_Subset(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run-partial.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	got := Intermediates(r, config.MaxInlineResultBytes)
	// Only journal entries 0 and 2 exist; agent callIndex 1 is still running.
	if len(got) != 2 {
		t.Fatalf("len(intermediate) = %d, want 2", len(got))
	}
	if got[0].Label != "claim A" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[0].Label = %q, want claim A", got[0].Label)
	}
	if got[1].Label != "claim C" {
		t.Errorf("intermediate[1].Label = %q, want claim C", got[1].Label)
	}
}

func TestIntermediates_TruncatesOverLimit(t *testing.T) {
	r, err := ReadRun(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ReadRun: %v", err)
	}
	// Force truncation with a tiny limit.
	got := Intermediates(r, 16)
	if len(got) == 0 {
		t.Fatal("no intermediates")
	}
	for i := range got {
		if !got[i].Truncated {
			t.Errorf("intermediate[%d].Truncated = false, want true (limit 16)", i)
		}
		if got[i].Preview == "" {
			t.Errorf("intermediate[%d].Preview empty, want a preview when truncated", i)
		}
		if len(got[i].Result) != 0 {
			t.Errorf("intermediate[%d].Result not dropped when truncated: %s", i, got[i].Result)
		}
	}
}

func TestIntermediates_UnmatchedJournalSkipped(t *testing.T) {
	r := &model.Run{
		Journal: []model.JournalEntry{
			{Index: 99, Result: json.RawMessage(`{"x":1}`)}, // no agent with callIndex 99
		},
		Agents: []model.Agent{
			{CallIndex: 0, ID: 1, Label: "a", Model: "m", Phase: "P"},
		},
	}
	got := Intermediates(r, config.MaxInlineResultBytes)
	if len(got) != 0 {
		t.Errorf("len(intermediate) = %d, want 0 (journal index 99 has no matching agent)", len(got))
	}
}
```
> Add `import "pi-mcp/internal/model"` to this test file's import group (used by the last subtest).

**R4.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestIntermediates
```
Expected FAIL: `undefined: Intermediates`.

**R4.3 — Minimal impl.** Write `internal/runstore/intermediate.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"pi-mcp/internal/model"
)

// Intermediates builds the live intermediate[] list for pi_status by joining
// each journal entry to its agent via journal[].Index == agents[].CallIndex
// (NEVER by array position — journal is in completion order; NEVER by
// agents[].ID, which equals CallIndex+1). The order of the returned slice
// follows journal order (completion order). Journal entries with no matching
// agent are skipped.
//
// Each entry carries the COMPLETE journal[].result. When that result exceeds
// maxBytes, the raw Result is dropped and a truncated UTF-8-safe Preview is set
// with Truncated=true.
func Intermediates(r *model.Run, maxBytes int) []model.IntermediateResult {
	byCallIndex := make(map[int]*model.Agent, len(r.Agents))
	for i := range r.Agents {
		byCallIndex[r.Agents[i].CallIndex] = &r.Agents[i]
	}

	out := make([]model.IntermediateResult, 0, len(r.Journal))
	for i := range r.Journal {
		j := &r.Journal[i]
		ag, ok := byCallIndex[j.Index] // JOIN: index == callIndex
		if !ok {
			continue
		}
		ir := model.IntermediateResult{
			Label: ag.Label,
			Model: ag.Model,
			Phase: ag.Phase,
		}
		if maxBytes > 0 && len(j.Result) > maxBytes {
			ir.Truncated = true
			ir.Preview = truncatePreview(string(j.Result), maxBytes)
			// Result left empty when truncated.
		} else {
			ir.Result = j.Result
		}
		out = append(out, ir)
	}
	return out
}

// truncatePreview returns s clipped to at most n bytes without splitting a
// multi-byte UTF-8 rune.
func truncatePreview(s string, n int) string {
	if n <= 0 {
		return ""
	}
	if len(s) <= n {
		return s
	}
	cut := n
	for cut > 0 && (s[cut]&0xC0) == 0x80 { // mid-rune continuation byte
		cut--
	}
	return s[:cut]
}
```

**R4.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestIntermediates -v
```
Expected PASS.

**R4.5 — Commit.**
```
git add internal/runstore/intermediate.go internal/runstore/intermediate_test.go
git commit -m "runstore: Intermediates joins journal.index<->agents.callIndex, truncates over limit"
```

**R5.3 — Minimal impl.** Write `internal/runstore/result.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"encoding/json"

	"pi-mcp/internal/model"
)

// StatusCompleted is the run-file status string for a finished run. runstore
// treats .result as authoritative only at this status (per §5.2/§7).
const StatusCompleted = "completed"

// AuthoritativeResult returns the run-file .result and true only when the run
// has completed and carries a non-empty result. Mid-run (running/paused/failed)
// the .result is not authoritative, so ok is false and callers should fall back
// to the live stream parser. The returned RawMessage aliases r.Result.
func AuthoritativeResult(r *model.Run) (json.RawMessage, bool) {
	if r.Status != StatusCompleted {
		return nil, false
	}
	if len(r.Result) == 0 || string(r.Result) == "null" {
		return nil, false
	}
	return r.Result, true
}

// Metadata builds the StatusMetadata block for pi_status: the by_model histogram,
// agent count, and (only when present in the run file) token usage and duration.
// TokenUsage and Cost are written by pi only at the end of a run, so they remain
// nil mid-run — Metadata never synthesizes or recomputes them (Cost is verbatim).
func Metadata(r *model.Run) model.StatusMetadata {
	return model.StatusMetadata{
		ByModel:    ModelHistogram(r),
		AgentCount: len(r.Agents),
		TokenUsage: r.TokenUsage, // nil until the run ends
		DurationMs: r.DurationMs, // nil until the run ends
	}
}
```

**R5.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run 'TestAuthoritativeResult|TestMetadata' -v
```
Expected PASS.

**R5.5 — Commit.**

```
git commit -m "runstore: AuthoritativeResult (completed only) + Metadata (cost/duration suppressed mid-run)"
```

## Task R6 — `ListRuns`: scan runs dir (exclude .bak/.tmp), sort updatedAt desc, build ListItem

**R6.1 — Build a runs-dir fixture tree.** The list test needs a directory with multiple run files plus excluded `.bak`/`.tmp`. Create it in the test via `t.TempDir()` (no committed fixture needed). Write `internal/runstore/list_test.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"
)

// writeRunsDir lays out a temp runs dir: the canonical completed run, the
// partial running run, plus a .bak and a .tmp that MUST be excluded from the glob.
func writeRunsDir(t *testing.T) string {
	t.Helper()
	dir := t.TempDir()
	copyFile := func(src, dstName string) {
		b, err := os.ReadFile(src)
		if err != nil {
			t.Fatalf("read %s: %v", src, err)
		}
		if err := os.WriteFile(filepath.Join(dir, dstName), b, 0o644); err != nil {
			t.Fatalf("write %s: %v", dstName, err)
		}
	}
	copyFile(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"), "mq40rdpt-yij9hj.json")
	copyFile(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run-partial.json"), "pq71abcd-partial.json")
	// Must be excluded:
	copyFile(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"), "ignored.json.bak")
	copyFile(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"), "ignored.json.tmp")
	return dir
}

func TestListRuns_SortAndFields(t *testing.T) {
	dir := writeRunsDir(t)
	out, err := ListRuns(dir, 20)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ListRuns: %v", err)
	}
	if len(out.Runs) != 2 {
		t.Fatalf("len(Runs) = %d, want 2 (.bak/.tmp excluded)", len(out.Runs))
	}
	// Both fixtures share updatedAt timestamp; sort is updatedAt desc, ties by
	// runId. "pq71abcd-partial" > "mq40rdpt-yij9hj" lexically, so it comes first.
	if out.Runs[0].RunID != "pq71abcd-partial" {
		t.Errorf("Runs[0].RunID = %q, want pq71abcd-partial (tie broken by runId)", out.Runs[0].RunID)
	}

	// Find the completed run and assert its derived fields.
	var completed *struct {
		idx int
	}
	for i := range out.Runs {
		if out.Runs[i].RunID == "mq40rdpt-yij9hj" {
			completed = &struct{ idx int }{i}
		}
	}
	if completed == nil {
		t.Fatal("completed run not in list")
	}
	c := out.Runs[completed.idx]
	if c.Status != "completed" {
		t.Errorf("completed.Status = %q, want completed", c.Status)
	}
	if c.WorkflowName != "judge_claims" {
		t.Errorf("completed.WorkflowName = %q, want judge_claims", c.WorkflowName)
	}
	if c.AgentCount != 4 {
		t.Errorf("completed.AgentCount = %d, want 4", c.AgentCount)
	}
	if c.ByModel["deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash"] != 3 || c.ByModel["openai-codex/gpt-5.5"] != 1 {
		t.Errorf("completed.ByModel = %v, want {flash:3, gpt-5.5:1}", c.ByModel)
	}
	if c.Cost == nil || *c.Cost != 0.1463847 {
		t.Errorf("completed.Cost = %v, want 0.1463847", c.Cost)
	}
	if c.DurationMs == nil || *c.DurationMs != 22391 {
		t.Errorf("completed.DurationMs = %v, want 22391", c.DurationMs)
	}
	if c.CompletedAt == nil {
		t.Errorf("completed.CompletedAt = nil, want non-nil")
	}

	// Find the partial (running) run: Cost/DurationMs/CompletedAt all nil.
	for i := range out.Runs {
		if out.Runs[i].RunID == "pq71abcd-partial" {
			p := out.Runs[i]
			if p.Status != "running" {
				t.Errorf("partial.Status = %q, want running", p.Status)
			}
			if p.Cost != nil {
				t.Errorf("partial.Cost = %v, want nil", p.Cost)
			}
			if p.DurationMs != nil {
				t.Errorf("partial.DurationMs = %v, want nil", p.DurationMs)
			}
			if p.CompletedAt != nil {
				t.Errorf("partial.CompletedAt = %v, want nil", p.CompletedAt)
			}
			if p.AgentCount != 3 {
				t.Errorf("partial.AgentCount = %d, want 3", p.AgentCount)
			}
		}
	}
}

func TestListRuns_LimitTruncates(t *testing.T) {

func TestListRuns_SkipsCorruptFileWithoutBak(t *testing.T) {
	dir := t.TempDir()
	if err := os.WriteFile(filepath.Join(dir, "broken.json"), []byte("{ not json"), 0o644); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("write: %v", err)
	}
	b, _ := os.ReadFile(filepath.Join("testdata", "sample-run.json"))
	if err := os.WriteFile(filepath.Join(dir, "good.json"), b, 0o644); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("write: %v", err)
	}
	out, err := ListRuns(dir, 20)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("ListRuns: %v", err)
	}
	if len(out.Runs) != 1 || out.Runs[0].RunID != "mq40rdpt-yij9hj" {
		t.Errorf("Runs = %+v, want only the good run (corrupt-without-.bak skipped)", out.Runs)
	}
}
```

**R6.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestListRuns
```
Expected FAIL: `undefined: ListRuns`.

**R6.3 — Minimal impl.** Write `internal/runstore/list.go`:
```go
package runstore

import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"
	"sort"
	"strings"
	"time"

	"pi-mcp/internal/model"
)

// ListRuns scans dir for *.json run files (excluding *.bak and *.tmp), decodes
// each (with .bak fallback on corrupt), and returns ListItems sorted by
// updatedAt descending (ties broken by runId for determinism), capped at limit.
// A missing dir yields an empty list and no error. Files that fail to decode and
// have no usable .bak are skipped (best-effort listing).
func ListRuns(dir string, limit int) (model.ListOutput, error) {
	entries, err := os.ReadDir(dir)
	if err != nil {
		if os.IsNotExist(err) {
			return model.ListOutput{Runs: []model.ListItem{}}, nil
		}
		return model.ListOutput{}, err
	}

	type scored struct {
		item    model.ListItem
		updated time.Time
	}
	var rows []scored
	for _, e := range entries {
		if e.IsDir() {
			continue
		}
		name := e.Name()
		if !strings.HasSuffix(name, ".json") {
			continue // also excludes *.json.bak / *.json.tmp via suffix check
		}
		// Defensive: skip anything that ended up as .bak/.tmp despite the suffix.
		if strings.HasSuffix(name, ".bak") || strings.HasSuffix(name, ".tmp") {
			continue
		}
		r, derr := ReadRun(filepath.Join(dir, name))
		if derr != nil {
			continue // corrupt without recoverable .bak — skip
		}
		rows = append(rows, scored{item: toListItem(r), updated: updatedAt(r)})
	}

	sort.SliceStable(rows, func(i, j int) bool {
		if rows[i].updated.Equal(rows[j].updated) {
			return rows[i].item.RunID > rows[j].item.RunID // deterministic tie-break
		}
		return rows[i].updated.After(rows[j].updated)
	})

	if limit > 0 && len(rows) > limit {
		rows = rows[:limit]
	}

	out := model.ListOutput{Runs: make([]model.ListItem, 0, len(rows))}
	for i := range rows {
		out.Runs = append(out.Runs, rows[i].item)
	}
	return out, nil
}

func updatedAt(r *model.Run) time.Time {
	if r.UpdatedAt != nil {
		return *r.UpdatedAt
	}
	return time.Time{} // missing updatedAt sorts last
}

// toListItem projects a Run into the pi_list row. Cost is the verbatim
// tokenUsage.cost (nil when tokenUsage is omitted, e.g. running/failed runs).
func toListItem(r *model.Run) model.ListItem {
	li := model.ListItem{
		RunID:        r.RunID,
		WorkflowName: r.WorkflowName,
		Status:       r.Status,
		AgentCount:   len(r.Agents),
		ByModel:      ModelHistogram(r),
		DurationMs:   r.DurationMs,
		CompletedAt:  r.CompletedAt,
	}
	if r.TokenUsage != nil {
		c := r.TokenUsage.Cost
		li.Cost = &c
	}
	return li
}
```

**R6.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runstore/ -run TestListRuns -v
```
Expected PASS.

**R6.5 — Commit.**
```

git commit -m "runstore: ListRuns scans runs dir (excl .bak/.tmp), sorts updatedAt desc, builds ListItem"
```

### Notes for the executor
- runstore is **pure**: I/O + decode + project. No status mapping (`running|paused`→`running`), no liveness/staleness, no PID checks — those are `internal/jobs`' job. runstore returns the **raw** run-file `Status` string; consumers map it.
- The JOIN is the load-bearing invariant: `journal[i].Index == agents[j].CallIndex`. Tested explicitly against the out-of-order canonical fixture (journal order 0,2,1,3) and the partial subset (0,2) so a regression to array-position or `id`-based joins fails loudly.
- `Cost` is verbatim `float64` everywhere (never recomputed); `Cost`/`DurationMs`/`TokenUsage`/`CompletedAt` stay nil mid-run, asserted by the partial fixture.
- If `internal/model` field names differ from the contract at integration time, that's a contract violation upstream — do NOT patch runstore to compensate; raise it against the model package owner.

## internal/worktree — write-mode git worktree lifecycle (create/diff/prune) (`worktree`)

**Files:** /root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/worktree.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/worktree_test.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/testhelper_test.go

_Assumptions:_ This package CONSUMES the foundation contract; it does NOT define model/config types. It uses `model.WriteInfo`, `model.ErrNotAGitRepo`, `config.WorktreeBranchPrefix` (="pi-mcp/job-"), and `config.WorktreeSubdir` (="pi-mcp/worktrees") exactly as given. If those packages are not yet present when implementing, add a temporary `// foundation-stub` const block (noted inline in W1/W3) and delete it once internal/config and internal/model land. files_touched lists only files this package authors.; git (>=2.39) is on PATH where `go test` runs (verified here: git 2.39.5). Go 1.23+ is installed in the implementation environment. Go is NOT installed in this planning sandbox, so the FAIL/PASS lines are the expected outputs when run on a Go-enabled machine, not executed here.; Worktree base resolution order: $XDG_STATE_HOME/pi-mcp/worktrees if XDG_STATE_HOME non-empty; else $HOME/.local/state/pi-mcp/worktrees; else os.TempDir()/pi-mcp/worktrees (XDG Base Directory spec; matches spec wording 'XDG_STATE/temp').; Worktree path = <base>/job-<jobId>; jobId is the server UUIDv4. Tests use deterministic synthetic ids. Branch = config.WorktreeBranchPrefix + jobId = pi-mcp/job-<jobId>.; Dirty/untracked HEAD = WARN + PROCEED (spec §4.1): branch is cut from committed HEAD; uncommitted user changes are NOT carried in. Create returns a non-fatal Handle.DirtyWarning string and never errors on dirtiness. Verified by W5 ('committed-HEAD-only' invariant: untracked files absent, tracked file at committed content).; diff_stat = `git -C <wt> diff --stat <BaseCommit>`; files_changed = `git -C <wt> diff --name-only -z <BaseCommit>` (NUL-split for paths with spaces/newlines). This compares the worktree (index+working tree) against the commit the branch started from, so it captures uncommitted edits made by write-mode agents. New files must be staged (`git add`) to appear in --name-only; the jobs/runner package is responsible for staging the worktree before calling Diff/WriteInfo (flagged in W6 NOTE). Empty diff => empty DiffStat + nil FilesChanged, not an error.; Collision: Create errors if branch pi-mcp/job-<jobId> OR target worktree dir already exists (no silent reuse). jobId global uniqueness is the jobs package's responsibility; worktree fails loudly on collision.; Prune is idempotent (W8): `git worktree remove --force` then os.RemoveAll fallback, `git branch -D` (ignore-absent), `git worktree prune`. PruneOrphans (W9) parses `git worktree list --porcelain`, removes only worktrees whose branch has the pi-mcp/job- prefix, preserves unrelated worktrees/branches, returns removed branch names. Both safe to call repeatedly (pi_cancel + startup reconciliation).; Every git call uses exec.CommandContext(ctx, ...) so pi_cancel can interrupt; not-a-repo detected up front via `git -C <cwd> rev-parse --is-inside-work-tree` != "true" => model.ErrNotAGitRepo. W10 locks the cancellation contract.; Tests build a throwaway repo under t.TempDir() with `git init -b main`, local user.email/user.name and commit.gpgsign=false (works in CI with no global identity). The worktree base is redirected into t.TempDir() via the exported test seam worktree.SetBaseDirForTest(t, dir) (backed by package var baseDirFn), so all worktrees are auto-cleaned and nothing leaks into $HOME/$XDG_STATE_HOME or the module tree. baseDirFn is the only test seam; production never reassigns it.; Test files live in `package worktree` (white-box) so they can exercise unexported helpers (resolveBaseDir, branchFor, branchExists) and the test seam. W2 is the single non-TDD scaffolding commit (helpers have no behavior to assert); W3 immediately exercises them under real assertions.

# Package W — internal/worktree

Write-mode isolation: create a git worktree OUTSIDE the user tree (under `$XDG_STATE_HOME/pi-mcp/worktrees/` or temp), on a fresh branch `pi-mcp/job-<jobId>` from HEAD, collision-checked. Fail fast with `NOT_A_GIT_REPO` when cwd is not a repo. Compute `diff_stat` + `files_changed` to fill `model.WriteInfo`. Prune/remove the worktree+branch on cancel/crash. All tests run inside a throwaway git repo created by the test itself.

**Foundation contract this package CONSUMES (does not define):**
- `model.WriteInfo struct{ Branch, WorktreePath, DiffStat string; FilesChanged []string }`
- `model.ErrNotAGitRepo` (string const = `"NOT_A_GIT_REPO"`)
- `config.WorktreeBranchPrefix` = `"pi-mcp/job-"`, `config.WorktreeSubdir` = `"pi-mcp/worktrees"`

**Public API this package PROVIDES (the contract the `jobs` + `mcpserver` packages build on):**
```go
package worktree

// Manager creates/diffs/prunes write-mode worktrees for a single repo cwd.
type Manager struct{ repoCWD string }

// New validates cwd is a git repo (else model.ErrNotAGitRepo) and returns a Manager.
func New(ctx context.Context, cwd string) (*Manager, error)

// Handle identifies one created worktree.
type Handle struct {
    JobID        string
    Path         string // absolute worktree path, OUTSIDE repoCWD
    Branch       string // pi-mcp/job-<jobId>
    BaseCommit   string // HEAD sha the branch was cut from
    DirtyWarning string // non-empty if HEAD had uncommitted/untracked changes (warn+proceed)
}

// Create makes branch pi-mcp/job-<jobId> from HEAD and a worktree at <base>/job-<jobId>.
// Collision (branch or dir exists) => error. Not-a-repo can't happen (New validated).
func (m *Manager) Create(ctx context.Context, jobID string) (*Handle, error)

// Diff returns DiffStat + FilesChanged for the worktree vs its BaseCommit (includes
// uncommitted edits in the worktree). Empty diff => empty/nil, not an error.
func (m *Manager) Diff(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) (diffStat string, filesChanged []string, err error)

// WriteInfo assembles the model.WriteInfo delivered in pi_status (write jobs).
func (m *Manager) WriteInfo(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) (model.WriteInfo, error)

// Prune removes one worktree + its branch idempotently (safe if already gone). For pi_cancel.
func (m *Manager) Prune(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) error

// PruneOrphans GCs every pi-mcp/job-* worktree+branch in the repo, then `git worktree prune`.
// For startup reconciliation. Returns the branches it removed.
func (m *Manager) PruneOrphans(ctx context.Context) ([]string, error)
```

**Conventions for every task below:**
- Working dir for `go test`: the module root `/root/pi-mcp`. All paths absolute.
- Run a single task's test with the exact command shown; expected FAIL (red) then PASS (green).
- Commit message footer (each commit): `Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 <noreply@anthropic.com>`.
- Test base-dir override: `worktree.go` resolves the base via a package var `baseDirFn func() (string, error)` (default = XDG resolver). Tests set `worktree.SetBaseDirForTest(t.TempDir())` so worktrees land in auto-cleaned temp dirs. This var is the ONLY test seam; production code never touches it.

## Task W1 — Package skeleton + base-dir resolver (XDG_STATE → HOME/.local/state → temp)

**W1.1 — Write the failing test** `/root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/worktree_test.go`:
```go
package worktree

import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"
	"strings"
	"testing"
)

func TestResolveBaseDir(t *testing.T) {
	tests := []struct {
		name    string
		xdg     string
		home    string
		wantSub string // suffix the result must end with
	}{
		{name: "xdg set", xdg: "/tmp/xdgstate", home: "/home/u", wantSub: filepath.Join("/tmp/xdgstate", "pi-mcp", "worktrees")},
		{name: "xdg empty falls to home", xdg: "", home: "/home/u", wantSub: filepath.Join("/home/u", ".local", "state", "pi-mcp", "worktrees")},
	}
	for _, tt := range tests {
		t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
			t.Setenv("XDG_STATE_HOME", tt.xdg)
			t.Setenv("HOME", tt.home)
			got, err := resolveBaseDir()
			if err != nil {
				t.Fatalf("resolveBaseDir() err = %v", err)
			}
			if got != tt.wantSub {
				t.Fatalf("resolveBaseDir() = %q, want %q", got, tt.wantSub)
			}
		})
	}
}

func TestResolveBaseDir_TempFallback(t *testing.T) {
	t.Setenv("XDG_STATE_HOME", "")
	t.Setenv("HOME", "")
	got, err := resolveBaseDir()
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("resolveBaseDir() err = %v", err)
	}
	if !strings.HasSuffix(got, filepath.Join("pi-mcp", "worktrees")) {
		t.Fatalf("temp fallback = %q, want suffix pi-mcp/worktrees", got)
	}
	if !strings.HasPrefix(got, os.TempDir()) {
		t.Fatalf("temp fallback = %q, want prefix %q", got, os.TempDir())
	}
}
```

**W1.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestResolveBaseDir' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `undefined: resolveBaseDir` (package does not compile yet).

**W1.3 — Minimal impl** `/root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/worktree.go`:
```go
// Package worktree manages write-mode git worktrees: it creates an isolated
// worktree OUTSIDE the user's working tree on a fresh pi-mcp/job-<id> branch,
// computes the delivered diff, and prunes worktrees+branches on cancel/crash.
package worktree

import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"

	"pi-mcp/internal/config"
)

// baseDirFn resolves the directory that holds all pi-mcp worktrees. It is a
// package var ONLY so tests can redirect worktrees into a temp dir via
// SetBaseDirForTest. Production code never reassigns it.
var baseDirFn = resolveBaseDir

// resolveBaseDir implements the XDG state resolution:
// $XDG_STATE_HOME/pi-mcp/worktrees -> $HOME/.local/state/pi-mcp/worktrees -> $TMPDIR/pi-mcp/worktrees.
func resolveBaseDir() (string, error) {
	if xdg := os.Getenv("XDG_STATE_HOME"); xdg != "" {
		return filepath.Join(xdg, config.WorktreeSubdir), nil
	}
	if home := os.Getenv("HOME"); home != "" {
		return filepath.Join(home, ".local", "state", config.WorktreeSubdir), nil
	}
	return filepath.Join(os.TempDir(), config.WorktreeSubdir), nil
}
```

> NOTE: `config.WorktreeSubdir` == `"pi-mcp/worktrees"`. `filepath.Join("/x", "pi-mcp/worktrees")` normalizes to `/x/pi-mcp/worktrees`, so the test suffix comparisons hold on POSIX. If the foundation `config` package is not yet present, temporarily add `const WorktreeSubdir = "pi-mcp/worktrees"` to a local `// foundation-stub` block at the top of `worktree.go` and delete it once `internal/config` lands. Do NOT redefine it in the real config package.

**W1.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestResolveBaseDir' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (both `TestResolveBaseDir` and `TestResolveBaseDir_TempFallback`).

**W1.5 — Commit:**
```
git add internal/worktree/worktree.go internal/worktree/worktree_test.go
git commit -m "worktree: base-dir resolver (XDG_STATE -> HOME -> temp)"
```

## Task W2 — Test helpers: throwaway git repo + base-dir seam

**W2.1 — Write the helper file** `/root/pi-mcp/internal/worktree/testhelper_test.go` (no assertions yet — utilities used by W3+; also adds the exported test seam consumed by `worktree.go`):
```go
package worktree

import (
	"context"
	"os"
	"os/exec"
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"
)

// SetBaseDirForTest redirects all worktree creation into dir for the duration
// of the test. Restored automatically via t.Cleanup.
func SetBaseDirForTest(t *testing.T, dir string) {
	t.Helper()
	prev := baseDirFn
	baseDirFn = func() (string, error) { return dir, nil }
	t.Cleanup(func() { baseDirFn = prev })
}

// git runs a git command in dir and fails the test on error, returning stdout.
func git(t *testing.T, dir string, args ...string) string {
	t.Helper()
	cmd := exec.Command("git", args...)
	cmd.Dir = dir
	out, err := cmd.CombinedOutput()
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("git %v in %s failed: %v\n%s", args, dir, err, out)
	}
	return string(out)
}

// newRepo creates a throwaway git repo under t.TempDir() with one commit and a
// deterministic identity (works in CI with no global git config). Returns cwd.
func newRepo(t *testing.T) string {
	t.Helper()
	dir := filepath.Join(t.TempDir(), "repo")
	if err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o755); err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	git(t, dir, "init", "-q", "-b", "main")
	git(t, dir, "config", "user.email", "test@pi-mcp.local")
	git(t, dir, "config", "user.name", "pi-mcp test")
	git(t, dir, "config", "commit.gpgsign", "false")
	writeFile(t, dir, "README.md", "hello\n")
	git(t, dir, "add", "-A")
	git(t, dir, "commit", "-q", "-m", "init")
	return dir
}

// writeFile writes name=content under dir (mkdir -p of parents).
func writeFile(t *testing.T, dir, name, content string) {
	t.Helper()
	p := filepath.Join(dir, name)
	if err := os.MkdirAll(filepath.Dir(p), 0o755); err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	if err := os.WriteFile(p, []byte(content), 0o644); err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
}

// ctx is a short helper for a background context in tests.
func ctx() context.Context { return context.Background() }
```

**W2.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestResolveBaseDir' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — compile error: `baseDirFn declared and not used`? No — `baseDirFn` is used by `resolveBaseDir`'s caller in later tasks; here the helper compiles but `newRepo`/`writeFile`/`ctx`/`git`/`SetBaseDirForTest` are unused in test build → Go test files tolerate unused package-level funcs, so this actually COMPILES and existing tests PASS. To force a red first, W2 has no new test; treat W2 as a refactor commit. If `go vet` flags nothing, proceed.

> Rationale: helper-only files have no behavior to test. W2 is the one allowed non-TDD commit (pure scaffolding). The very next task (W3) exercises these helpers under a real assertion.

**W2.3 — Run (expect PASS, sanity):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (W1 tests still green; helpers compile).

**W2.4 — Commit:**
```

git commit -m "worktree: test helpers (throwaway repo, base-dir seam)"
```

## Task W3 — `New`: validate cwd is a git repo, else NOT_A_GIT_REPO

**W3.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
import "pi-mcp/internal/model" // add to the import block

func TestNew_NotAGitRepo(t *testing.T) {
	dir := t.TempDir() // plain dir, never `git init`ed
	_, err := New(ctx(), dir)
	if err == nil {
		t.Fatal("New() on non-repo: want error, got nil")
	}
	if err.Error() != model.ErrNotAGitRepo {
		t.Fatalf("New() err = %q, want %q", err.Error(), model.ErrNotAGitRepo)
	}
}

func TestNew_NestedNonRepoSubdir(t *testing.T) {
	// A dir that is NOT inside any repo (temp dir is outside the module repo).
	sub := filepath.Join(t.TempDir(), "a", "b")
	if err := os.MkdirAll(sub, 0o755); err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	if _, err := New(ctx(), sub); err == nil || err.Error() != model.ErrNotAGitRepo {
		t.Fatalf("New() nested non-repo err = %v, want %q", err, model.ErrNotAGitRepo)
	}
}

func TestNew_ValidRepo(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	m, err := New(ctx(), repo)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("New() on valid repo err = %v", err)
	}
	if m == nil {
		t.Fatal("New() returned nil Manager")
	}
}
```

**W3.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestNew' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `undefined: New`.

**W3.3 — Minimal impl** (append to `worktree.go`; add imports `context`, `os/exec`, `strings`, `errors`, `pi-mcp/internal/model`):
```go
// Manager creates/diffs/prunes write-mode worktrees for a single repo cwd.
type Manager struct {
	repoCWD string
}

// New verifies cwd is inside a git work tree. If not, it returns an error whose
// message is exactly model.ErrNotAGitRepo (the catalog code), so callers fail
// fast before spawning pi.
func New(ctx context.Context, cwd string) (*Manager, error) {
	cmd := exec.CommandContext(ctx, "git", "-C", cwd, "rev-parse", "--is-inside-work-tree")
	out, err := cmd.CombinedOutput()
	if err != nil || strings.TrimSpace(string(out)) != "true" {
		return nil, errors.New(model.ErrNotAGitRepo)
	}
	return &Manager{repoCWD: cwd}, nil
}
```

> NOTE: `git -C <missingdir> rev-parse` exits non-zero AND a dir with no `.git` (and no parent repo) prints `false`/errors — both branches map to `model.ErrNotAGitRepo`. If the foundation `model` package isn't present yet, add `const ErrNotAGitRepo = "NOT_A_GIT_REPO"` to the `// foundation-stub` block and remove it once `internal/model` lands.

**W3.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestNew' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (all three `TestNew*`).

**W3.5 — Commit:**
```
git add internal/worktree/worktree.go internal/worktree/worktree_test.go
git commit -m "worktree: New() validates git repo, else NOT_A_GIT_REPO"
```

## Task W4 — `Create`: fresh branch `pi-mcp/job-<id>` from HEAD + worktree OUTSIDE the tree

**W4.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
func TestCreate_BranchAndPathOutsideTree(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	base := t.TempDir()
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, base)

	m, err := New(ctx(), repo)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	h, err := m.Create(ctx(), "job-1234")
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Create() err = %v", err)
	}

	// Branch name follows config.WorktreeBranchPrefix.
	if h.Branch != "pi-mcp/job-job-1234" {
		t.Fatalf("Branch = %q, want pi-mcp/job-job-1234", h.Branch)
	}
	// Worktree path is under the (test) base dir, NOT under the repo cwd.
	if !strings.HasPrefix(h.Path, base) {
		t.Fatalf("Path %q not under base %q", h.Path, base)
	}
	if strings.HasPrefix(h.Path, repo) {
		t.Fatalf("Path %q must be OUTSIDE repo %q", h.Path, repo)
	}
	// The worktree dir exists and contains the committed file.
	if _, err := os.Stat(filepath.Join(h.Path, "README.md")); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("worktree missing README.md: %v", err)
	}
	// git lists the new worktree.
	out := git(t, repo, "worktree", "list", "--porcelain")
	if !strings.Contains(out, h.Path) {
		t.Fatalf("git worktree list missing %q:\n%s", h.Path, out)
	}
	// BaseCommit equals repo HEAD.
	head := strings.TrimSpace(git(t, repo, "rev-parse", "HEAD"))
	if h.BaseCommit != head {
		t.Fatalf("BaseCommit = %q, want HEAD %q", h.BaseCommit, head)
	}
}

func TestCreate_Collision(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	if _, err := m.Create(ctx(), "dup"); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("first Create err = %v", err)
	}
	if _, err := m.Create(ctx(), "dup"); err == nil {
		t.Fatal("second Create with same jobID: want collision error, got nil")
	}
}
```

**W4.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestCreate' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `h.Create undefined (type *Manager has no field or method Create)` / `Handle undefined`.

**W4.3 — Minimal impl** (append to `worktree.go`; add import `fmt`):
```go
// Handle identifies one created write-mode worktree.
type Handle struct {
	JobID        string
	Path         string // absolute worktree path, OUTSIDE repoCWD
	Branch       string // pi-mcp/job-<jobId>
	BaseCommit   string // HEAD sha the branch was cut from
	DirtyWarning string // non-empty when HEAD had uncommitted/untracked changes
}

// branchFor builds the fresh branch name for a job.
func branchFor(jobID string) string { return config.WorktreeBranchPrefix + jobID }

// Create cuts branch pi-mcp/job-<jobID> from HEAD and adds a worktree at
// <base>/job-<jobID>, OUTSIDE the user's working tree. A pre-existing branch or
// target dir is a collision (error). HEAD dirtiness is recorded as a warning
// (warn+proceed) on the returned Handle; it never fails Create.
func (m *Manager) Create(ctx context.Context, jobID string) (*Handle, error) {
	base, err := baseDirFn()
	if err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("resolve worktree base: %w", err)
	}
	if err := os.MkdirAll(base, 0o755); err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("mkdir worktree base: %w", err)
	}
	path := filepath.Join(base, "job-"+jobID)
	branch := branchFor(jobID)

	// Collision: target dir already present.
	if _, statErr := os.Stat(path); statErr == nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("worktree path already exists: %s", path)
	}
	// Collision: branch already present.
	if exists, berr := m.branchExists(ctx, branch); berr != nil {
		return nil, berr
	} else if exists {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("branch already exists: %s", branch)
	}

	head, err := m.runGit(ctx, "rev-parse", "HEAD")
	if err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("rev-parse HEAD: %w", err)
	}
	head = strings.TrimSpace(head)

	warn := m.dirtyWarning(ctx)

	// `git worktree add -b <branch> <path> HEAD` creates the branch from HEAD
	// and checks it out into the new worktree in one shot.
	if _, err := m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "add", "-b", branch, path, "HEAD"); err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("worktree add: %w", err)
	}

	return &Handle{
		JobID:        jobID,
		Path:         path,
		Branch:       branch,
		BaseCommit:   head,
		DirtyWarning: warn,
	}, nil
}

// branchExists reports whether refs/heads/<branch> is present.
func (m *Manager) branchExists(ctx context.Context, branch string) (bool, error) {
	cmd := exec.CommandContext(ctx, "git", "-C", m.repoCWD, "show-ref", "--verify", "--quiet", "refs/heads/"+branch)
	err := cmd.Run()
	if err == nil {
		return true, nil
	}
	if ee, ok := err.(*exec.ExitError); ok && ee.ExitCode() == 1 {
		return false, nil // exit 1 = ref absent
	}
	return false, fmt.Errorf("show-ref %s: %w", branch, err)
}

// dirtyWarning returns a non-empty warning if HEAD has staged/unstaged/untracked
// changes (warn+proceed: those changes are NOT carried into the worktree).
func (m *Manager) dirtyWarning(ctx context.Context) string {
	out, err := m.runGit(ctx, "status", "--porcelain")
	if err != nil {
		return ""
	}
	if strings.TrimSpace(out) != "" {
		return "HEAD has uncommitted/untracked changes; worktree branched from committed HEAD only"
	}
	return ""
}

// runGit runs a git subcommand in repoCWD and returns combined output.
func (m *Manager) runGit(ctx context.Context, args ...string) (string, error) {
	full := append([]string{"-C", m.repoCWD}, args...)
	cmd := exec.CommandContext(ctx, "git", full...)
	out, err := cmd.CombinedOutput()
	if err != nil {
		return string(out), fmt.Errorf("git %v: %w (%s)", args, err, strings.TrimSpace(string(out)))
	}
	return string(out), nil
}
```

**W4.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestCreate' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (both `TestCreate_BranchAndPathOutsideTree` and `TestCreate_Collision`).

**W4.5 — Commit:**
```

git commit -m "worktree: Create() fresh branch from HEAD, worktree outside tree, collision-checked"
```

## Task W5 — Dirty/untracked HEAD → warn + proceed (no error)

**W5.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
func TestCreate_DirtyHeadWarnsProceeds(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())

	// Leave an uncommitted + untracked change in the repo HEAD.
	writeFile(t, repo, "README.md", "hello dirty\n") // modify tracked
	writeFile(t, repo, "scratch.txt", "untracked\n")  // add untracked

	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, err := m.Create(ctx(), "dirty1")
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Create() on dirty HEAD must proceed, got err = %v", err)
	}
	if h.DirtyWarning == "" {
		t.Fatal("DirtyWarning empty; want a non-empty warn on dirty HEAD")
	}
	// The worktree reflects committed HEAD only: README is the committed "hello",
	// and the untracked file is absent.
	got, err := os.ReadFile(filepath.Join(h.Path, "README.md"))
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	if string(got) != "hello\n" {
		t.Fatalf("worktree README = %q, want committed %q", got, "hello\n")
	}
	if _, err := os.Stat(filepath.Join(h.Path, "scratch.txt")); !os.IsNotExist(err) {
		t.Fatalf("untracked file leaked into worktree (err=%v)", err)
	}
}

func TestCreate_CleanHeadNoWarn(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, err := m.Create(ctx(), "clean1")
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}
	if h.DirtyWarning != "" {
		t.Fatalf("clean HEAD DirtyWarning = %q, want empty", h.DirtyWarning)
	}
}
```

**W5.2 — Run (expect PASS — behavior already implemented in W4):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestCreate_(DirtyHeadWarnsProceeds|CleanHeadNoWarn)' -v
```
Expected: `PASS`. (W4 already wired `dirtyWarning`; this task LOCKS the warn+proceed contract with explicit tests and the "committed-HEAD-only" invariant. If it fails, fix `dirtyWarning`/ordering in `worktree.go` before moving on — `status --porcelain` must run BEFORE `worktree add`.)

## Task W6 — `Diff`: diff_stat + files_changed vs BaseCommit (captures uncommitted worktree edits)

**W6.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
func TestDiff_CapturesWorktreeEdits(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, err := m.Create(ctx(), "diff1")
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatal(err)
	}

	// Simulate write-mode agents editing the shared job worktree: one modified,
	// one new file. Do NOT commit — Diff must see uncommitted worktree changes.
	writeFile(t, h.Path, "README.md", "hello\nmore\n")
	writeFile(t, h.Path, "src/new.go", "package src\n")
	git(t, h.Path, "add", "-A") // stage so untracked new file shows in name-only

	diffStat, files, err := m.Diff(ctx(), h)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Diff() err = %v", err)
	}
	if !strings.Contains(diffStat, "README.md") {
		t.Fatalf("diffStat missing README.md:\n%s", diffStat)
	}
	wantFiles := map[string]bool{"README.md": true, "src/new.go": true}
	for _, f := range files {
		delete(wantFiles, f)
	}
	if len(wantFiles) != 0 {
		t.Fatalf("files_changed missing %v; got %v", wantFiles, files)
	}
}

func TestDiff_EmptyWhenNoChanges(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, _ := m.Create(ctx(), "empty1")

	diffStat, files, err := m.Diff(ctx(), h)
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Diff() err = %v", err)
	}
	if strings.TrimSpace(diffStat) != "" {
		t.Fatalf("empty diff stat = %q, want empty", diffStat)
	}
	if len(files) != 0 {
		t.Fatalf("empty files_changed = %v, want none", files)
	}
}
```

**W6.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestDiff' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `m.Diff undefined`.

**W6.3 — Minimal impl** (append to `worktree.go`):
```go
// Diff returns the git --stat output and the list of changed files for the
// worktree, comparing the worktree's index+working tree against BaseCommit so
// that uncommitted edits made by write-mode agents are captured. An empty diff
// yields ("", nil, nil), not an error.
func (m *Manager) Diff(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) (string, []string, error) {
	// --stat against BaseCommit, including staged + unstaged changes.
	statOut, err := runGitIn(ctx, h.Path, "diff", "--stat", h.BaseCommit)
	if err != nil {
		return "", nil, fmt.Errorf("diff --stat: %w", err)
	}
	// NUL-delimited name list (safe for paths with spaces/newlines).
	nameOut, err := runGitIn(ctx, h.Path, "diff", "--name-only", "-z", h.BaseCommit)
	if err != nil {
		return "", nil, fmt.Errorf("diff --name-only: %w", err)
	}
	var files []string
	for _, f := range strings.Split(nameOut, "\x00") {
		if f != "" {
			files = append(files, f)
		}
	}
	return strings.TrimRight(statOut, "\n"), files, nil
}

// runGitIn runs git in an arbitrary dir (used for worktree-local commands).
func runGitIn(ctx context.Context, dir string, args ...string) (string, error) {
	full := append([]string{"-C", dir}, args...)
	cmd := exec.CommandContext(ctx, "git", full...)
	out, err := cmd.CombinedOutput()
	if err != nil {
		return string(out), fmt.Errorf("git %v: %w (%s)", args, err, strings.TrimSpace(string(out)))
	}
	return string(out), nil
}
```

> NOTE: `git diff <commit>` (no `--cached`) shows working-tree vs commit, which includes staged AND unstaged tracked changes. New files must be `git add`-staged to appear in `--name-only` (matching how pi's write agents stage edits, or how the runner stages before delivery). The test stages with `git add -A` to model this; the jobs/runner package is responsible for staging before calling Diff/WriteInfo (note this in the jobs package plan).

**W6.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestDiff' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (both `TestDiff_CapturesWorktreeEdits` and `TestDiff_EmptyWhenNoChanges`).

**W6.5 — Commit:**
```

git commit -m "worktree: Diff() diff_stat + files_changed vs BaseCommit (NUL-safe)"
```

```go
// WriteInfo assembles the model.WriteInfo returned by pi_status for write jobs:
// branch, worktree path, diff --stat, and the changed-file list.
func (m *Manager) WriteInfo(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) (model.WriteInfo, error) {
	diffStat, files, err := m.Diff(ctx, h)
	if err != nil {
		return model.WriteInfo{}, err
	}
	return model.WriteInfo{
		Branch:       h.Branch,
		WorktreePath: h.Path,
		DiffStat:     diffStat,
		FilesChanged: files,
	}, nil
}
```

## Task W8 — `Prune`: idempotent remove of one worktree + branch (pi_cancel)

**W8.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
func TestPrune_RemovesWorktreeAndBranch(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, _ := m.Create(ctx(), "prune1")

	// Add uncommitted changes — Prune must force-remove despite a dirty worktree.
	writeFile(t, h.Path, "README.md", "dirty before prune\n")

	if err := m.Prune(ctx(), h); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("Prune() err = %v", err)
	}
	// Worktree dir gone.
	if _, err := os.Stat(h.Path); !os.IsNotExist(err) {
		t.Fatalf("worktree dir still present (err=%v)", err)
	}
	// Branch gone.
	if exists, _ := m.branchExists(ctx(), h.Branch); exists {
		t.Fatalf("branch %s still present after Prune", h.Branch)
	}
	// git worktree list no longer references it.
	out := git(t, repo, "worktree", "list", "--porcelain")
	if strings.Contains(out, h.Path) {
		t.Fatalf("git worktree list still has %q:\n%s", h.Path, out)
	}
}

func TestPrune_Idempotent(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	h, _ := m.Create(ctx(), "prune2")

	if err := m.Prune(ctx(), h); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("first Prune err = %v", err)
	}
	// Second prune on an already-removed handle must be a no-op (no error).
	if err := m.Prune(ctx(), h); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("second Prune (idempotent) err = %v", err)
	}
}
```

**W8.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestPrune' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `m.Prune undefined`.

**W8.3 — Minimal impl** (append to `worktree.go`):
```go
// Prune force-removes the worktree at h.Path, deletes its branch, and runs
// `git worktree prune`. It is idempotent: a missing worktree or branch is not an
// error, so pi_cancel and startup reconciliation can call it safely.
func (m *Manager) Prune(ctx context.Context, h *Handle) error {
	// Force-remove the worktree (ignore "is not a working tree" / not found).
	_, _ = m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "remove", "--force", h.Path)
	// As a belt-and-suspenders, drop the dir if git left it behind.
	if _, err := os.Stat(h.Path); err == nil {
		_ = os.RemoveAll(h.Path)
	}
	// Delete the branch (ignore "branch not found").
	_, _ = m.runGit(ctx, "branch", "-D", h.Branch)
	// Reap administrative files for removed worktrees.
	if _, err := m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "prune"); err != nil {
		return fmt.Errorf("worktree prune: %w", err)
	}
	return nil
}
```

**W8.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestPrune' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (both `TestPrune_RemovesWorktreeAndBranch` and `TestPrune_Idempotent`).

**W8.5 — Commit:**
```
git add internal/worktree/worktree.go internal/worktree/worktree_test.go
git commit -m "worktree: Prune() idempotent remove of worktree+branch (pi_cancel)"
```

## Task W9 — `PruneOrphans`: GC every pi-mcp/job-* worktree+branch (startup reconciliation)

**W9.1 — Write the failing test** (append to `worktree_test.go`):
```go
func TestPruneOrphans_RemovesAllJobWorktrees(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)

	h1, _ := m.Create(ctx(), "orph-a")
	h2, _ := m.Create(ctx(), "orph-b")
	// A non-pi-mcp worktree + branch that MUST be preserved.
	other := filepath.Join(t.TempDir(), "other-wt")
	git(t, repo, "worktree", "add", "-b", "feature/keep", other, "HEAD")

	removed, err := m.PruneOrphans(ctx())
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("PruneOrphans() err = %v", err)
	}
	// Both pi-mcp branches reported as removed.
	gotRemoved := map[string]bool{}
	for _, b := range removed {
		gotRemoved[b] = true
	}
	if !gotRemoved[h1.Branch] || !gotRemoved[h2.Branch] {
		t.Fatalf("removed = %v, want both %s and %s", removed, h1.Branch, h2.Branch)
	}
	// pi-mcp worktree dirs gone.
	for _, h := range []*Handle{h1, h2} {
		if _, err := os.Stat(h.Path); !os.IsNotExist(err) {
			t.Fatalf("orphan worktree %s still present", h.Path)
		}
		if exists, _ := m.branchExists(ctx(), h.Branch); exists {
			t.Fatalf("orphan branch %s still present", h.Branch)
		}
	}
	// The unrelated worktree + branch survived.
	if _, err := os.Stat(other); err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("non-pi-mcp worktree wrongly removed: %v", err)
	}
	if exists, _ := m.branchExists(ctx(), "feature/keep"); !exists {
		t.Fatal("non-pi-mcp branch feature/keep wrongly removed")
	}
}

func TestPruneOrphans_NoneIsNoError(t *testing.T) {
	repo := newRepo(t)
	SetBaseDirForTest(t, t.TempDir())
	m, _ := New(ctx(), repo)
	removed, err := m.PruneOrphans(ctx())
	if err != nil {
		t.Fatalf("PruneOrphans() with no orphans err = %v", err)
	}
	if len(removed) != 0 {
		t.Fatalf("removed = %v, want none", removed)
	}
}
```

**W9.2 — Run (expect FAIL):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestPruneOrphans' -v
```
Expected: `FAIL` — `m.PruneOrphans undefined`.

**W9.3 — Minimal impl** (append to `worktree.go`; add import `bufio`, `strings` already present):
```go
// PruneOrphans removes every worktree whose branch starts with
// config.WorktreeBranchPrefix ("pi-mcp/job-"), deletes those branches, and runs
// `git worktree prune`. It leaves unrelated worktrees/branches untouched. Used by
// startup reconciliation to GC worktrees orphaned by a crash. Returns the list of
// branches removed.
func (m *Manager) PruneOrphans(ctx context.Context) ([]string, error) {
	out, err := m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "list", "--porcelain")
	if err != nil {
		return nil, fmt.Errorf("worktree list: %w", err)
	}

	type wt struct{ path, branch string }
	var found []wt
	var cur wt
	sc := bufio.NewScanner(strings.NewReader(out))
	for sc.Scan() {
		line := sc.Text()
		switch {
		case strings.HasPrefix(line, "worktree "):
			cur = wt{path: strings.TrimPrefix(line, "worktree ")}
		case strings.HasPrefix(line, "branch "):
			// e.g. "branch refs/heads/pi-mcp/job-abc"
			cur.branch = strings.TrimPrefix(strings.TrimPrefix(line, "branch "), "refs/heads/")
		case line == "": // blank line terminates one worktree record
			if cur.path != "" {
				found = append(found, cur)
			}
			cur = wt{}
		}
	}
	if cur.path != "" { // last record with no trailing blank
		found = append(found, cur)
	}

	var removed []string
	for _, w := range found {
		if !strings.HasPrefix(w.branch, config.WorktreeBranchPrefix) {
			continue
		}
		_, _ = m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "remove", "--force", w.path)
		if _, err := os.Stat(w.path); err == nil {
			_ = os.RemoveAll(w.path)
		}
		_, _ = m.runGit(ctx, "branch", "-D", w.branch)
		removed = append(removed, w.branch)
	}
	if _, err := m.runGit(ctx, "worktree", "prune"); err != nil {
		return removed, fmt.Errorf("worktree prune: %w", err)
	}
	return removed, nil
}
```

**W9.4 — Run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/worktree/ -run 'TestPruneOrphans' -v
```
Expected: `PASS` (both subtests).

**W9.5 — Commit:**
```
git add internal/worktree/worktree.go internal/worktree/worktree_test.go
git commit -m "worktree: PruneOrphans() GC pi-mcp/job-* worktrees, preserve others"
```

```go
func TestCreate_CanceledContext(t *testing.T) {
```

## Coverage map (spec §10 "worktree: cria/lista/diff num repo de teste; fora do tree; NOT_A_GIT_REPO; prune no cancel")
- **cria** → W4 (`Create`, branch from HEAD, outside tree), W5 (dirty warn+proceed)
- **lista/diff** → W6 (`Diff` diff_stat + files_changed), W7 (`WriteInfo` → `model.WriteInfo`)
- **fora do tree** → W1 (XDG base resolver), W4 (`Path` prefix asserts OUTSIDE repo)
- **NOT_A_GIT_REPO** → W3 (`New` validates, error == `model.ErrNotAGitRepo`)
- **prune no cancel** → W8 (`Prune` idempotent), W9 (`PruneOrphans` startup GC), W10 (ctx cancel)

## internal/runner — spawn pi subprocess (argv, prompt rendering, stdin=/dev/null, env passthrough, cwd, context-kill) (`runner`)

**Files:** /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/prompt.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/prompt_test.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/argv.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/argv_test.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/runner.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/runner_test.go, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/testdata/fake-pi.sh, /root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/testdata/fake-pi-fixture.jsonl, /root/pi-mcp/internal/config/config.go

_Assumptions:_ go is NOT installed in this build environment (verified: `go version` -> command not found). All `go test` commands in this plan are written to be run where Go 1.23+ IS installed. Task N1 includes a Go-presence check.; The runner depends on `pi-mcp/internal/config` for PiBinary, PiBaseFlags, NoContextFilesFlag, DefaultNoContextFiles, ForcingPromptTemplate, ReadContractSkeleton, WriteContractSkeleton. Per the shared contract these consts live in internal/config and are OWNED by the config package author. This plan defines them in config.go ONLY IF that file/consts do not already exist when this package is implemented; the implementer must NOT clobber a config.go authored by the config-package task — if it exists, reuse its consts verbatim and skip Task N2's config.go write (the values here match the contract exactly so either source is interchangeable).; ForcingPromptTemplate uses placeholders {{CONTRACT}}, {{TASK}}, {{CONTEXT}} (per shared contract). The exact prose of the template body is taken from §4.2 of the spec and docs/research/fixtures/sample-forced-workflow-prompt.txt. The renderer does literal placeholder substitution; when context is empty the entire `\n\n[CONTEXT:\n{{CONTEXT}}]` bracketed block is omitted (the §4.2 template shows CONTEXT as optional in [brackets]).; ReadContractSkeleton and WriteContractSkeleton are the §5.4 JSON shape skeletons substituted into {{CONTRACT}}. Exact JSON text defined in config.go below; they are descriptive shapes (not strict JSON to be parsed), matching §5.4.; The runner spawns via os/exec with cmd.Stdin set to an *os.File opened on os.DevNull (/dev/null). It does NOT use a nil Stdin (which would inherit the parent's stdin and risk the documented hang). Tests assert the fake pi sees an EOF/empty stdin.; The runner exposes a Spawn function that returns a started *exec.Cmd plus an io.ReadCloser for stdout so the caller (jobs package) wires stdout to the parser. Kill is achieved by passing a context.Context to exec.CommandContext; cancelling the context kills the process. This matches the spec's 'kill via context (for cancel)'.; stderr is captured to a caller-provided io.Writer (diagnostic only, per §4); the runner itself does not log it. Tests pass a bytes.Buffer.; The fake pi is a POSIX shell script (testdata/fake-pi.sh) made executable and placed on PATH via the test setting PATH for the child only (the test points PiBinary indirectly by invoking the script through an absolute path override). To keep the runner faithful to PiBinary="pi", Spawn takes the binary name from config.PiBinary, and the test prepends the testdata dir to PATH and symlinks/copies the script to a file named `pi` in a temp dir on PATH. Assumed `sh`, `printf`, `cat`, `test` available on the test host.; go.mod module path is `pi-mcp` (per shared contract MODULE: pi-mcp), so import paths are `pi-mcp/internal/config`.; Commits use git; the repo is initialized by an earlier foundation task. If `git` reports 'not a repository' when running these tasks standalone, run `git init` first (out of scope for this package).

# Package N — internal/runner

Spawns the `pi` subprocess for each job: renders the §4.2 forcing prompt (template + §5.4 contract skeleton + task/context), builds argv (`pi -p --mode json --no-session [--no-context-files] <single positional prompt>`), starts the process with **stdin=/dev/null** (CRITICAL), **env=os.Environ()** passthrough, and the job **cwd** (project for read / worktree for write), exposes stdout to the parser, and supports **kill via context** (for `pi_cancel`).

Tested end-to-end with a **fake `pi`** (a tiny POSIX shell script on `PATH`) that asserts stdin is empty (/dev/null), echoes back its argv/cwd/env into a sentinel file, and emits a fixture JSONL stream on stdout. We assert: prompt rendering, argv shape, stdin=/dev/null, env passthrough, cwd, stdout streaming, and context-kill.

**Shared types/consts used (do not redefine elsewhere):** `config.PiBinary`, `config.PiBaseFlags`, `config.NoContextFilesFlag`, `config.DefaultNoContextFiles`, `config.ForcingPromptTemplate`, `config.ReadContractSkeleton`, `config.WriteContractSkeleton`. Mode strings `"read"`/`"write"` are `model.ModeRead`/`model.ModeWrite` per §8.

Otherwise create the minimal file the runner needs.

```

```
**Expected (if config not yet written):** no matches → proceed to Step 2. **If matches found:** STOP this task; the consts exist.

**Step 2 — write `/root/pi-mcp/internal/config/config.go`** (only the runner-relevant subset; the config-package task owns the full file — merge, don't clobber):
```go
package config

// pi invocation contract (§4).
const PiBinary = "pi"

var PiBaseFlags = []string{"-p", "--mode", "json", "--no-session"}

const NoContextFilesFlag = "--no-context-files"

// DefaultNoContextFiles: default OFF (false) per shared contract; callers may flip per-job.
const DefaultNoContextFiles = false

// ForcingPromptTemplate (§4.2). Placeholders: {{CONTRACT}}, {{TASK}}, {{CONTEXT}}.
// The bracketed CONTEXT block is removed by the renderer when context is empty.
const ForcingPromptTemplate = `You MUST make exactly ONE call to the ` + "`workflow`" + ` tool with background:false. Do not answer
directly. Do not use background:true. Return the final synthesized result INLINE this turn.
Decompose the task as you see fit and fan out subagents in parallel.
The workflow MUST return an object matching exactly this JSON shape:
{{CONTRACT}}

TASK:
{{TASK}}

[CONTEXT:
{{CONTEXT}}]`

// ReadContractSkeleton / WriteContractSkeleton (§5.4): requested output shapes.
const ReadContractSkeleton = `{ "summary": string, "findings": [{ "title": string, "detail": string, "severity"?: "low"|"med"|"high" }], "confidence": string, "open_questions": [string] }`

const WriteContractSkeleton = `{ "summary": string, "files_changed": [string], "diff_summary": string, "tests_run"?: string, "notes": string }`
```

**Step 3 — build/vet:**
```
go build ./internal/config/
```
**Expected:** PASS (no output, exit 0).

**Step 4 — commit:**
```
git add internal/config/config.go
git commit -m "config: pi invocation consts + forcing prompt template (runner deps)

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 <noreply@anthropic.com>"
```

## Task N3 — RenderPrompt: failing test (read mode, with context)

**Step 1 — write `/root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/prompt_test.go`:**
```go
package runner

import (
	"strings"
	"testing"

	"pi-mcp/internal/config"
)

func TestRenderPrompt(t *testing.T) {
	tests := []struct {
		name        string
		mode        string
		task        string
		context     string
		wantContains []string
		wantAbsent   []string
	}{
		{
			name:    "read with context",
			mode:    "read",
			task:    "Audit auth flow",
			context: "focus on session.go",
			wantContains: []string{
				"You MUST make exactly ONE call",
				"background:false",
				config.ReadContractSkeleton,
				"TASK:\nAudit auth flow",
				"CONTEXT:\nfocus on session.go",
			},
			wantAbsent: []string{
				"{{CONTRACT}}", "{{TASK}}", "{{CONTEXT}}",
				config.WriteContractSkeleton,
			},
		},
		{
			name:    "write without context omits bracket block",
			mode:    "write",
			task:    "Add retry to client",
			context: "",
			wantContains: []string{
				config.WriteContractSkeleton,
				"TASK:\nAdd retry to client",
			},
			wantAbsent: []string{
				"{{CONTRACT}}", "{{TASK}}", "{{CONTEXT}}",
				"CONTEXT:", "[CONTEXT", config.ReadContractSkeleton,
			},
		},
	}
	for _, tt := range tests {
		t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
			got, err := RenderPrompt(tt.mode, tt.task, tt.context)
			if err != nil {
				t.Fatalf("RenderPrompt error: %v", err)
			}
			for _, sub := range tt.wantContains {
				if !strings.Contains(got, sub) {
					t.Errorf("prompt missing %q\n--- prompt ---\n%s", sub, got)
				}
			}
			for _, sub := range tt.wantAbsent {
				if strings.Contains(got, sub) {
					t.Errorf("prompt should NOT contain %q\n--- prompt ---\n%s", sub, got)
				}
			}
		})
	}
}

func TestRenderPromptBadMode(t *testing.T) {
	if _, err := RenderPrompt("delete", "t", ""); err == nil {
		t.Fatal("expected error for invalid mode, got nil")
	}
}
```

**Step 2 — run (expect FAIL: RenderPrompt undefined):**
```
go test ./internal/runner/ -run TestRenderPrompt
```
**Expected:** FAIL — `undefined: RenderPrompt` (compile error).

## Task N4 — RenderPrompt: minimal impl

**Step 1 — write `/root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/prompt.go`:**
```go
package runner

import (
	"fmt"
	"strings"

	"pi-mcp/internal/config"
)

// RenderPrompt builds the single positional prompt (§4.2) from the forcing
// template, the §5.4 contract skeleton for the mode, the task, and optional
// context. TASK/CONTEXT are inserted as delimited data, never as executable
// script (the engine vm is not a security sandbox — §14).
//
// When context is empty the entire "[CONTEXT:\n...]" bracket block is removed,
// matching the optional-bracket form in the §4.2 template.
func RenderPrompt(mode, task, context string) (string, error) {
	var contract string
	switch mode {
	case "read":
		contract = config.ReadContractSkeleton
	case "write":
		contract = config.WriteContractSkeleton
	default:
		return "", fmt.Errorf("runner: invalid mode %q (want \"read\" or \"write\")", mode)
	}

	out := config.ForcingPromptTemplate
	out = strings.Replace(out, "{{CONTRACT}}", contract, 1)
	out = strings.Replace(out, "{{TASK}}", task, 1)

	if strings.TrimSpace(context) == "" {
		// Remove the optional bracketed CONTEXT block, including the blank
		// line that precedes it, leaving a clean prompt tail.
		out = stripContextBlock(out)
	} else {
		out = strings.Replace(out, "{{CONTEXT}}", context, 1)
	}
	return out, nil
}

// stripContextBlock removes the "[CONTEXT:\n{{CONTEXT}}]" block (and the blank
// line separating it from TASK) from the rendered template when no context is
// supplied. It is resilient to the {{CONTEXT}} placeholder being present.
func stripContextBlock(s string) string {
	idx := strings.Index(s, "[CONTEXT:")
	if idx < 0 {
		return s
	}
	head := s[:idx]
	// Trim trailing whitespace/newlines left by removing the block.
	return strings.TrimRight(head, "\n ")
}
```

**Step 2 — run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runner/ -run TestRenderPrompt
```
**Expected:** PASS — `ok  	pi-mcp/internal/runner`. Both subtests and `TestRenderPromptBadMode` green.

**Step 3 — commit:**
```

git commit -m "runner: RenderPrompt (forcing template + contract skeleton + task/context)

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 <noreply@anthropic.com>"
```

```go
package runner

import (
	"reflect"
	"testing"
)

func TestBuildArgv(t *testing.T) {
	prompt := "THE PROMPT\nwith newline"
	tests := []struct {
		name          string
		noContextFiles bool
		want          []string
	}{
		{
			name:           "no context-files flag when false",
			noContextFiles: false,
			want:           []string{"pi", "-p", "--mode", "json", "--no-session", "THE PROMPT\nwith newline"},
		},
		{
			name:           "context-files flag when true",
			noContextFiles: true,
			want:           []string{"pi", "-p", "--mode", "json", "--no-session", "--no-context-files", "THE PROMPT\nwith newline"},
		},
	}
	for _, tt := range tests {
		t.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {
			got := BuildArgv(prompt, tt.noContextFiles)
			if !reflect.DeepEqual(got, tt.want) {
				t.Errorf("BuildArgv mismatch\n got: %#v\nwant: %#v", got, tt.want)
			}
		})
	}
}

// The prompt must be exactly ONE argv element (no shell, no splitting on spaces/newlines).
func TestBuildArgvPromptIsSingleElement(t *testing.T) {
	prompt := "multi word\nmulti line prompt"
	got := BuildArgv(prompt, false)
	last := got[len(got)-1]
	if last != prompt {
		t.Fatalf("prompt not preserved as single argv element\n got: %q\nwant: %q", last, prompt)
	}
}
```

## Task N6 — BuildArgv: minimal impl

**Step 1 — write `/root/pi-mcp/internal/runner/argv.go`:**
```go
package runner

import "pi-mcp/internal/config"

// BuildArgv assembles the full argv for the pi subprocess (§4):
//
//	pi -p --mode json --no-session [--no-context-files] <single positional prompt>
//
// argv[0] is config.PiBinary; the prompt is appended as exactly ONE element
// (no shell, no escaping; newlines preserved). When noContextFiles is true the
// config.NoContextFilesFlag is inserted before the positional prompt.
func BuildArgv(prompt string, noContextFiles bool) []string {
	argv := make([]string, 0, len(config.PiBaseFlags)+3)
	argv = append(argv, config.PiBinary)
	argv = append(argv, config.PiBaseFlags...)
	if noContextFiles {
		argv = append(argv, config.NoContextFilesFlag)
	}
	argv = append(argv, prompt)
	return argv
}
```

**Step 2 — run (expect PASS):**
```
go test ./internal/runner/ -run TestBuildArgv
```
**Expected:** PASS — both subtests + `TestBuildArgvPromptIsSingleElement` green.

```
git commit -m "runner: BuildArgv (pi base flags + optional --no-context-files + single positional prompt)

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.8 <noreply@anthropic.com>"
```
